>
> **Code Keywords:** else. (1), let (1), module (1), default, (1)
> **Definitions:** in other words (1), means that (1)
> **Best Practices:** recommended (2)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Speakers:** - authentication (1)

#### Role-Based vs Claims-Based Authorization
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=0)** - When planning out your security strategy for your applications, two methods can be used.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=6)** Role-based authorization or claims-based authorization.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=11)** Let's take a look at each.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=13)** In Role-based authorization, applications enforce access by roles.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=19)** These roles can be used in authorized attributes in your code.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=24)** Alternatively, claims-based authorization enforces permissions by using information about the user rather than relying on a single role declaration.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=36)** These pieces of information are called claims, and are passed along as part of a user identity.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=42)** Claims are more granular, and can be customized to include relevant information that your application needs.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=49)** Let's say you wanted to authorize a loyalty discount to users that are part of your rewards program.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=55)** With claims-based authorization, you could create a claim called reward program member ID.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=61)** Then, you could authorize the discount for the users who have this claim as a part of their user identity.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=68)** Those who don't, probably aren't rewards program members, and won't get an additional 30% off.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=75)** To best understand the difference between these two, let's take a look at role-based and claims-based authorization in a different way.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=84)** When we go to the airport, most of us line up to go through a security checkpoint.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=89)** Every now and then, we see pilots and cabin crew skip ahead through a designated line.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=95)** In order to get through that line, individuals must have a proper badge that states they are, in fact, a pilot or other cabin crew member.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=104)** This is very similar to how role-based authorization works.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=108)** Because those passing through are pilots, flight attendants, or other valid cabin crew roles, they are given the authorization to move through this line.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=118)** And the badges that hold their respective titles are the roles security agents use to give them the approval.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=125)** Meanwhile, the rest of us are still waiting in line to get through the security checkpoint.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=130)** We can't use that other line as we're just plain old travelers.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=134)** We aren't pilots or cabin crew, and we don't have a badge.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=138)** What we do have, however, are several pieces of information about who we are, a boarding pass, and a form of identification.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=146)** These items are like claims.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=149)** They'll tell the security agent who we are, and they'll use them to determine whether or not we're authorized to proceed.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=156)** Once we finally get to the security agent, they'll compare the boarding pass and ID we provide to the airport's authorization scheme.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=165)** If they can match a traveler in their system to the same full name and flight on our boarding pass, and to the ID we provide as valid, we can proceed.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=175)** In general, it's advised not to code against specific roles and applications as this makes them tightly coupled, and difficult to change.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=184)** I've gone through this mistake before.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=186)** It's not a fun process to re-architect your application security.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=191)** Have you ever assumed a certain role was going to stay the same, or get to a point where two people with the same role needed varying levels of authorization?
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=200)** That's what happened in my case.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=203)** We had a sales role that was widely used within our application.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=207)** When a few more members joined the sales team, they were assigned this sales role.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=212)** Not too long after, a few members on the sales team needed read-only access, while others needed read and write access.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=221)** Because our authorization strategy was built around roles, the only way we could do this was to create even more roles.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=229)** (sighs) This wasn't scalable.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=232)** In fact, we should've built authorization around the actions performed on our platform instead of the people performing them.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=241)** This was especially true in our case as many people in our company overlapped in functionality, but not in role.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=249)** So as you're thinking about access control for your applications, don't make the same mistake I did.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/role-based-vs-claims-based-authorization?u=76281980&t=255)** In almost all scenarios, the flexibility of claims-based authorization is a much better strategy.

> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **UI Navigation:** go to (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)

#### What is Azure Key Vault?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=0)** - Have you ever come across sensitive information like critical API keys or user credentials just laying around?
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=8)** Or maybe you've committed sensitive information to your own repos?
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=14)** It's okay.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=15)** I won't tell anyone.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=17)** Hopefully the consequences of these scenarios are apparent to you.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=22)** When critical pieces of our applications are exposed or are easier to get to, the more insecure our applications really are.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=30)** That's why it's especially important for us as developers to ensure these parts of our application are secure.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=38)** This is where Azure Key Vault comes in.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=40)** Just like it sounds, Key Vault is a centralized place to store all kinds of sensitive information that your application might need.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=48)** Things like API keys, tokens, connection strings, and passwords can all be stored and managed in the Azure Key Vault, which means you can remove it from your application's code.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=59)** What's extremely convenient is that when we do need this information, we can use the Key Vault API to retrieve it.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=67)** And since it is part of the Azure ecosystem, Key Vault integrates with other services that you may be using.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=74)** For example, if you use Azure Disk Encryption to provide volume encryption for data disks, you can use Key Vault to store and manage your disk encryption keys and secrets.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=85)** Or if you manage certificates for your Azure app services, you can use Azure Key Vault to manage those certificates and import them directly into your app service.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=95)** The Azure for Developers: Security Best Practices course goes into deeper detail about how to integrate with the Azure Key Vault and how to use the Key Vault API.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-azure-key-vault?u=76281980&t=106)** If you have more complex scenarios to implement, or just want to learn more, I suggest checking it out.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** api (4)
> **Analogies:** just like (1), for example (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)
> **Speakers:** - have (1)


### 10. 9. Monitoring your applications

#### Using Azure Monitor
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=0)** - Once we've built our applications and deployed them to the world, our work isn't finished.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=7)** When users start interacting with our applications, there are many things about those interactions that we may want to keep track of.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=14)** And when things go wrong, we certainly want to know.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=18)** Azure Monitor is a full platform of tools that help us keep an eye on our applications.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=24)** It's a centralized solution for collecting, analyzing, and acting on the telemetry data we feed into it.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=31)** Telemetry data comes from a few sources.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=34)** It can come from the application itself which includes data about the performance and functionality of the code we write.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=41)** Or it can come from the operating system on which your application is running.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=46)** Finally, it can come from Azure resource, subscription, or tenant monitoring data which includes information about the operations of those resources and services.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=57)** Once collected, this data is split into metrics and logs.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=63)** Metrics are values used to describe some part of a system at a given point in time.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=69)** Logs are records of various types of data and are much more verbose than metrics.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=76)** Using just these two types of input, Azure Monitor can perform many functions.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=83)** As developers, Azure Monitor's insights and respond functions will be the most meaningful.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=89)** If you've ever needed to handle a production fire, you know how intimidating and overwhelming it can be.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=95)** When it happens, we just want to find the root cause or at least some meaningful error to start with, and then we can begin the debugging process.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=104)** Application insights is one of those tools that can make a big difference in those initial diagnosis phases.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=111)** Falling under the insights function of Azure Monitor, application insights watches a range of things about our application.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=119)** It can tell us whether our app services are available, or how long they've been down, show us the number of client error and server error statuses our application has sent within the last hour, and other useful points of data.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=133)** Now when you'd rather be proactive about your applications availability and performance, alerts are a key piece to your monitoring efforts.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=142)** By choosing a resource to watch and specifying criteria to look out for, you can use alerts to set up something called an alert rule.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=151)** These rules, when triggered, can be configured to perform an action, and that action is up to you.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=158)** Say your database admin should be alerted when your production database server CPU spikes over 80%.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=165)** With an alert rule, you'd choose the appropriate production database as your target resource.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=171)** Set the criteria to CPU usage being greater than 80%, and specify the action to take as a text message sent immediately to your database admin.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=181)** In my case, that's Chris.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=184)** These kinds of alerts could mean the difference between an "I need coffee every hour because "production is on fire" week or a normal, boring, but everything's working week.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=198)** There's a bunch more alert mechanisms you can set up, and not all of them need to be metric based.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-monitor?u=76281980&t=203)** Check out the alerts overview page to see them all.

#### What is Application Insights?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=0)** - Application Insights is a service that helps us understand how our applications are doing and how it's being used.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=8)** It's easy to add to your applications too.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=11)** By importing the Application Insights package to your project, you give yourself the ability to really observe your apps.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=18)** Once installed, Application Insights starts tracking important things about your app.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=23)** Things like request rates, response times and failure rates.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=27)** Which can help you find out which pages are the most popular.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=30)** At what times of the day and where your users are.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=34)** Or application exceptions, where you can drill into stack trace and related requests.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=40)** Page views, load performance and user end session counts are also tracked, which are key to accessing your applications performance, user engagement and user retention.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=51)** And if you need just a bit more customization, you can even write some code to track the events and metrics you care about.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=59)** Like cupcakes sold or least liked cat video.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=62)** All of this data and much more is continuously sent over to Azure Monitor to help you make sense of it all.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=69)** Since there's so much valuable information tracked by Application Insights, it's usually the first place I look when I need to diagnose production issues.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=78)** I'd specifically check to see if there are any HTTP errors reported and if so, which ones.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=85)** When I find plausible offenders, I drill into these errors and inspect the stack trace, review the other requests made before and after the errored one and check the performance and usage of related resources while the error occurred.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=100)** I think my favorite part about using Application Insights is that it's well integrated into Visual Studio and Azure Boards.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=108)** The moment an error occurs, or when I hopefully find the root cause of the bug that's happening in production, I can quickly create a task for it and immediately add it to the current sprint.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=119)** And this way, tracking is so much easier and streamlined.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=123)** And by quickly creating a task, which is linked to a work item or bug I can easily follow my teams rule of always linking a commit to the task that it's fulfilling.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=132)** There's so much more you can do with Application Insights, it's ridiculous.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/what-is-application-insights?u=76281980&t=137)** If you haven't already, add the Application Insights package to your project and start watching those sweet metrics come in.

### 11. 10. Optimizing your applications

#### Using Azure Redis for caching
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=0)** - As applications rely on more data, the potential to greatly slow down our app becomes a bigger risk.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=7)** This can happen as the data we wait for usually needs to be retrieved from our database.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=13)** But not all data has to be retrieved fresh each time it's needed.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=18)** That's why it's very much encouraged to implement caching with our applications, especially with data we know we'll need later on.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=27)** Azure Cache for Redis is the Azure-based implementation of Redis, a popular software used for caching.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=34)** It's a great way to implement caching with our Azure applications.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=39)** When we specify which data to cache, this data is temporarily copied into a FAST storage area.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=47)** This area is typically the end memory storage with Azure Cache.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=52)** As you can guess, our data retrieval process is now much faster, as we can go directly to this cache instead of doing a full query on our database.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=61)** With Azure Cache for Redis, there are a few common patterns we can use to fully take advantage of caching.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=68)** First, we have the cache-aside pattern.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=71)** In this pattern, we load data items into the cache only as needed and as our application makes changes to our database, this cache can also be updated at the same time.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=83)** This is kind of like putting aside some pastries at a bakery if we knew our parents were stopping by.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=92)** Since we'd want to make sure that our favorite cupcakes are available, we'd keep them close.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=98)** And when they inevitably change their mind, we can put the cupcakes back, or, you know, we could eat them.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=108)** If we don't update the cache at the same time that actual changes are made, we can still make sure our cache eventually gets updated using expiration rules.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=118)** These time-based rules can be set to force-update data to be reloaded into the cache.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=124)** Next is the content caching pattern.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=127)** This is great for static content that doesn't change very often or shouldn't be dynamically generated.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=134)** Website menus and footers are great examples of this kind of content.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=139)** By placing these kinds of things in Azure Cache for Redis, processing times and server load would decrease significantly.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=146)** Another pattern is called user session caching.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=151)** As you've probably seen, maybe even too often with the current GDPR regulations, this pattern commonly uses cookies to store information about a user.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=162)** With Azure Cache for Redis, we can offload information we'd normally store in the user cookie to the cache and use the cookie as a unique key instead.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=173)** Back to our bakery.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=175)** Say Dennis calls ahead and places an order for some macrons.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=181)** Oh, then Natalie calls in and orders a chocolate cupcake with sprinkles and a vanilla cupcake.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=188)** And at the last minute, Scott also calls in and places an order for two cupcakes.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=196)** Instead of remembering all of that information from scratch, we'd probably pull aside those orders, place them into some nice boxes, and label each one with the appropriate name.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=208)** This label is similar to the key used in our cache.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=212)** Searching by name, we can easily find each person's order super fast.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=218)** As you've seen, caching is a great way to make your data-heavy applications faster.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=224)** We've even seen a few of the patterns you can use to implement caching with Azure Cache for Redis.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-azure-redis-for-caching?u=76281980&t=230)** If you're excited to put these patterns into practice, check out this tutorial from Azure, where you'll create a leader board using the cache-aside pattern.

#### Using the Azure Content Delivery Network
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=0)** - Remember when websites loaded like this?
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=4)** Can you imagine the image heavy, super personalized and network request-laden websites of today loading in this way?
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=14)** I didn't think so.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=16)** I'm sure you're quite aware of how important fast load times are, they can make or break the user experience.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=23)** If you're developing applications that have a lot of media, dynamically generated content or content that can't be cached, the Azure Content Delivery Network is something you need.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=35)** The Azure Content Delivery Network, or Azure CDN for short, is a globally distributed network of servers designed to get content to users fast.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=46)** It works like any other CDN, which temporarily copies content to a location that's closer to the content's requester.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=54)** Unlike every other CDN, the Azure CDN offers additional features that make it an awesome CDN to use with your applications.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=64)** The first is Dynamic Site Acceleration.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=68)** Dynamic Site Acceleration solves the problem that exists with content that can't be cached.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=74)** It does this by focusing on how to get the content faster, since it can't take advantage of the cache.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=81)** One technique Dynamic Site Acceleration uses is route optimization.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=87)** Within the vast, ever-changing network of the internet the best route to the requested content's origin is determined and used.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=95)** This helps avoid unnecessarily long routes and common points of internet congestion.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=101)** Dynamic Site Acceleration also uses a feature called Adaptive Image Compression.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=108)** Since it's already monitoring network quality, this feature automatically compresses full resolution images based on the current network speed.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=117)** Another feature Azure CDN offers is HTTPS support for custom domains.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=123)** Sending sensitive data to your users securely is just common sense, and with Azure CDN you can turn on HTTPS support immediately.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=133)** And for your standard CDN endpoints, which are the URLs pointing to your files, HTTPS is enabled by default.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=142)** The last neat feature of Azure CDN is the ability to geo-filter requests.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=147)** With the geo-filtering feature, you can allow or block specific content in countries or regions that you choose.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=155)** You can do so by setting up rules on your CDN endpoint's pass.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=160)** CDNs are pretty much a standard component of most websites.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/using-the-azure-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=164)** To make sure your media-heavy websites perform their best, I'd encourage you to integrate the Azure CDN into your Azure App Services today.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>

#### Kubernetes Service scaling strategies
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=0)** - As you run applications in Azure Kubernetes Service, the compute resources you need will vary from time to time.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=7)** Ideally, they'd scale as demand increases and decreases, and it would all be done automatically.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=14)** Let's take a look at some of the scaling strategies that you can use with Azure Kubernetes Service.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=20)** As always, you can manually scale pods or nodes.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=24)** This is a great way to experiment with your application's responses to changes in its available resources.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=30)** If you explicitly set the amount of resources that can used, you can be sure that your costs are fixed as the Azure Kubernetes Service will comply to those amounts.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=42)** And that's pretty much how manually scaling works, you set the limits and then Azure Kubernetes Service makes sure those limits are followed.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=51)** Another way to scale is by using the Horizontal Pod Autoscaler.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=56)** As expected, Kubernetes detects when there's more demand for your application than your currently available resources can handle.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=65)** When this happens, it uses its Horizontal Pod Autoscaler to increase the number of replicas.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=71)** Replicas are copies of the pods your application is running on, and pods are the logical structure that hosts your containers.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=81)** It can detect required changes like this because the Horizontal Pod Autoscaler checks the Metrics API every 30 seconds.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=89)** For finer control, try setting your minimum and maximum number of replicas that can run in your deployments.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=96)** Occasionally, scale events may not have completed successfully before another check with the Metrics API is made.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=104)** This could cause the Horizontal Pod Autoscaler to incorrectly scale your replicas up or down.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=111)** In order to combat this, cool down or delay values are set.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=116)** These are values that tell the Horizontal Pod Autoscaler how long to wait before another scale event can be started.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=123)** By default, the delay on scale up events is three minutes, while the delay on scale down events is five minutes.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=131)** Unfortunately, these defaults can't be customized.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=135)** Lastly, there's the cluster autoscaler.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=138)** It's highly recommended to use the cluster autoscaler and Horizontal Pod Autoscaler together, as they work hand-in-hand.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=147)** As the number of replicas increase or decrease, thanks to changes by the Horizontal Pod Autoscaler, the cluster autoscaler proportionately adjusts the number of nodes needed to actually run those replicas.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=160)** The cluster Autoscaler checks the Metrics API every 10 seconds for changes in required node count.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/kubernetes-service-scaling-strategies?u=76281980&t=168)** Keep these strategies in mind as you experiment with the scaling options that are right for you.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>

> **Env Vars:** api (3)
> **CLI Commands:** node (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)

### 12. 11. AI in Azure

#### Azure AI and Responsible AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Is your AI responsible?
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=3)** I don't mean eating a healthy diet or recycling.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=8)** I mean is your usage, development, and deployment of AI done responsibly?
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=16)** As we adapt and integrate AI into our day-to-day workflows, it's imperative that we have guidelines we can follow while we go on this AI journey together.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=28)** In this video, we'll discuss what responsible AI is and why it's important.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=34)** We'll also learn about the six responsible AI principles that define the Microsoft Responsible AI Standard and how they can guide our AI development and use.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=48)** So what is responsible AI?
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=52)** Microsoft proposes it as a safe, trustworthy, and ethical approach to developing, assessing, and deploying AI systems.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=63)** While the use and development of AI is moving at light speed, the laws, norms, and policies surrounding AI, some of which we don't even know we need yet, are still catching up.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=76)** In order to answer some of the inevitable questions and fill in the gaps that are surfacing, establishing guidelines for AI was necessary.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=86)** Using the expertise from Microsoft's Research Policy and engineering teams over multiple years, six principles were established and shared to enable everyone to develop and deploy AI responsibly.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=100)** Let's talk about those six principles.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=104)** First is accountability.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=107)** This principle states that people should be accountable for AI systems.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=112)** It also asks us to consider how we can create oversight over AI systems so that humans can be accountable and in control.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=121)** In practice, implementing the principle of accountability can include assessment, review, and continuous updates of the impact of the AI system on people, organizations, and society.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=135)** Regular review of and additional oversight and requirements for systems that may have a significant adverse impact on people, organizations, and society.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=148)** Documented and defined purpose for the AI system, including how the system's use will solve the problem posed by each intended use, data governance and management of datasets used by the AI system, and the availability of human oversight and control with these AI systems.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=172)** The next principle is transparency.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=175)** This principle states that AI systems should be understandable and asks us to consider how we can ensure that people correctly understand the capabilities of an AI system.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=189)** Some ways to apply the principle of transparency include clear communication and capabilities and limitations of an AI system, and disclosing to those using an AI system that they are interacting with an AI system, or are using one that generates or manipulates image, audio, or video content that could falsely appear to be authentic.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=216)** Third is the principle of fairness.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=220)** This principle states that AI systems should treat all people fairly.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=225)** It also asks us to deliberate on how an AI system might allocate opportunities, resources, and information in ways that are fair to the humans who use it.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=238)** In practice, this means designing systems that provide a similar quality of service for identified demographic groups, including marginalized groups, making sure AI systems that allocate resources or opportunities in essential domains do so in a manner that minimizes disparities in outcomes for said groups, and minimizing outputs that contribute to the stereotyping, demeaning, or erasing of identified groups.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=272)** Reliability and safety is the fourth principle that states AI systems should perform reliably and safely.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=282)** Here we consider how an AI system might function well for people across different use conditions and contexts, including ones that it wasn't originally intended for.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=295)** Implementing this principle means ensuring reliability and safety guidance surrounding an AI system, including the evaluation of operational factors and ranges within which they're expected to perform, minimizing the time to remediation of predictable or known failures, and establishing ongoing monitoring, feedback, and evaluation of the AI system to identify and review new use cases, identify and troubleshoot issues, manage and maintain the system, and improve them over time.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=333)** Privacy and security is the fifth principle.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=337)** It states that AI systems should be secure and respect privacy, and asks us to contemplate on how an AI system might be designed to support privacy and security.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=351)** This includes designing systems to protect privacy in accordance with the Microsoft Privacy Standard and to be secure in accordance with the Microsoft Security Policy.
>
> **[6:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=365)** Finally, the last principle is inclusiveness.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=369)** This principle states AI systems would empower everyone and engage all people, regardless of their backgrounds.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=378)** It asks us to think about how to design an AI system that is inclusive for people of all abilities.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=387)** Applying this principle means designing AI systems that are inclusive in accordance with the Microsoft Accessibility Standards.
>
> **[6:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-and-responsible-ai?u=76281980&t=396)** Keeping the six Responsible AI Principles in mind while designing and developing AI systems, we can be confident that the systems we create are safe, trustworthy, and as ethical as possible.

>

>

>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=285)** While Azure AI Services offer a lower barrier to entry for common AI tasks with pre-built models, you might be sacrificing the ability to create more custom or complex functions or model training.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=300)** If that's the case, you might need to combine the pre-built models with something like Azure Machine Learning, which requires more specialized expertise.
>

>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=316)** The effectiveness of any AI model is completely dependent on the quality of your data.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=322)** Be prepared for challenges related to data ingestion, cleaning, and ensuring data quality Tools like Microsoft Purview can help.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=331)** Also be aware of model decay.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=335)** AI models can degrade over time as data patterns shift, a phenomenon known as data drift.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=342)** Continuous monitoring and a feedback loop between users and technical teams are vital to maintain accuracy.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=350)** Finally, ethical AI practices cannot be an afterthought.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=356)** This includes addressing potential biases in your datasets, ensuring fairness, and considering the user experience and ethical implications of your AI solution.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=369)** With the help of Azure AI Services, you can build intelligent applications faster and more efficiently.
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=377)** And keeping the considerations of security, cost, data quality, and ethical implications in mind, you can take advantage of Azure AI Services capabilities confidently.

#### Azure Machine Learning
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Had your fill of pre-built, ready-to-use AI models?
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=4)** Need to build something completely unique to your situation?
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=9)** Then, Azure Machine Learning might be what you're looking for.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=14)** In this video, I'll take you through what Azure Machine Learning is, when to use it, and how you would use it to manage the lifecycle of creating your own custom model.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=27)** So what exactly is Azure Machine Learning?
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=31)** It's a cloud-based platform that allows you to build, train, deploy, and manage machine learning models at scale.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=41)** This differs from Azure AI Services, which use pre-built, ready-to-use AI models.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=47)** Instead, Azure Machine Learning, or Azure ML for short, is intended for custom model development.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=56)** If you need to build a model from scratch, have specific requirements, or work with open-source frameworks, like PyTorch, TensorFlow, or scikit-learn, Azure ML is what you'll want to use as well.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=71)** Overall, Azure ML is an ML ops platform, meaning it helps you manage the entire machine learning lifecycle, from experimentation to production.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=83)** Now, let's break down how you would build a custom model using Azure ML.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=89)** Your custom model's journey starts with setting up your workspace.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=95)** This will be the main hub for all of your ML assets: experiments, compute resources, datasets, models, and endpoints.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=107)** Next, you'll need to acquire and prepare your data.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=112)** Using Azure ML, you can explore, clean, transform, and pre-process your raw data.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=119)** This includes tasks like understanding your raw data's structure and types, handling missing values or removing duplicates, or encoding categorical variables, to make sure your data is in the right format and quality for training.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=136)** One cool thing, you can define data assets in Azure ML, which allow you to version your dataset and have version references to your data.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=146)** This is key for reproducibility, as you'll always know which version of data was used for a specific model run.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=155)** With your data ready, you'll now decide your training method.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=159)** Will you go with a code-first or low-code approach?
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=164)** In a code-first approach, you write your training scripts in Python or R using the Python SDK or the Azure CLI, then run them on compute resources.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=176)** In a low-code approach, you can use Azure ML Designer, a drag-and-drop visual interface to build and train models without writing the code yourself.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=187)** After selecting a training method, you'll define your environment and compute.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=193)** Defining your environment means explicitly describing the software environment your model needs, as well as any dependencies, like Conda or Docker containers.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=204)** It's similar to a requirements file or a package.json file where you can explicitly set which version of libraries and packages to use.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=214)** This helps ensure reproducibility no matter where your model is run.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=219)** Say goodbye to, "It works on my machine," issues.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=225)** Defining your compute target means choosing where your code will run.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=230)** It establishes the computational power allocated for your ML tasks, whether that's for development, training, or inference.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=239)** You can think of it like provisioning a VM or Kubernetes cluster, but specifically focused on machine learning workloads.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=247)** You can decide from single-node, cloud-based dev environments called compute instances, scalable, multi-node clusters of VMs designed for distributed training and processing larger datasets, called compute clusters, or for basic tasks, plain old serverless compute.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=267)** With everything in place, you train, evaluate, and register your custom model next.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=275)** This means submitting your training job, likely multiple times with different configurations, and tracking experiment metrics and parameters with MLflow.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=286)** Out of these runs, you evaluate which model performed the best and register it in the model registry, a central repository for versioning and managing your models.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=300)** When you are ready to deploy a trained model, you take your static model file, such as a .pk1 or .onnx file, and make it available as a callable service for real-time predictions or batch processing.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=315)** As you use your trained model, a critical, ongoing last step is to monitor your model.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=322)** Specifically, you'll want to keep an eye on model performance and something called data drift.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=329)** Data drift refers to the change in the distribution of your model's input data over time, which can decrease the model's accuracy.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=339)** This feedback loop is crucial for knowing when to retrain your models.
>
> **[5:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=345)** Azure Machine Learning gives you the full control and capabilities to innovate with custom AI solutions.
>
> **[5:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=352)** It provides the ecosystem to take your models from ideation to production, manage them at scale, and continually improve their performance.

> **Env Vars:** sdk (1), cli (1)
> **Definitions:** is an  (1), refers to (1)
