### 13. 12. Interesting Advancements for Developers

#### Load testing on Azure App Service
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Speaker] Ensuring your application can handle real-world user traffic is crucial for a smooth and reliable user experience.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=8)** Load testing helps us achieve that by simulating various traffic patterns and loads to identify a performance bottlenecks and potential breaking points.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=18)** By the end of this video, you'll understand the importance of load testing.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=23)** You'll also learn how to create and run load tests directly from the Azure portal specifically within your app service instance.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=30)** Imagine your newly launched application suddenly experiences a surge in users due to a viral video.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=38)** Without proper load testing, you might encounter several issues.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=42)** Most common is slow response times.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=46)** Users might experience delays leading to a frustrating and poor user-experience, or worse potential abandonment.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=54)** Another issue is application crashes.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=58)** Under heavy load, your application might become unstable and crash resulting in downtime and data loss.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=66)** Resource exhaustion is another issue to expect.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=70)** Your app service plan might hit resource limits like CPU, memory or network limits, causing performance degradation for all applications hosted on that plan.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=82)** With load testing, identifying bottlenecks becomes easier as you can pinpoint specific parts of your application that may be causing performance issues under load.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=94)** By proactively load testing, you can identify these issues before they impact your users, allowing you to optimize your application and infrastructure for resilience and scalability.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=106)** The load testing feature integrated within Azure App Service allows you to generate synthetic-user traffic to your application and observe its performance metrics directly within the portal.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=118)** This simplified setup means you don't have to configure external load testing tools.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=124)** The configuration is done directly within the app service blade.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=129)** Behind the scenes, the feature uses the Azure Load Testing service, which provides the power and scale you'll need for your testing infrastructure and key performance indicators like response time, requests per second and error rates are displayed in real-time during the test.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=148)** One thing to keep in mind, running load tests does incur costs associated with the Azure load testing service.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=156)** In order to stay within budget, be mindful of the test duration and the number of virtual users configured.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=164)** Now let's see how you would set up Azure app service load testing in the portal.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=171)** First, ensure that you have the necessary requisites.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=175)** You'll need an application deployed to Azure App Service, which will be what you will load test.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=182)** You'll also need an active Azure subscription to access the Azure portal and app service features, and you'll need a basic understanding of your applications architecture.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=194)** Knowing the different components of your app and their interactions will help you interpret the load tests effectively.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=201)** After validating, you have the required prerequisites, open the Azure portal and locate your app service instance.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=214)** In the left-hand navigation menu of your app service blade.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=218)** Scroll down and expand the performance section.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=221)** Then click on load testing.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=225)** On the load testing page, click on the create test button and then create a URL-based test.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=234)** Here, you'll first outline your test plan.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=238)** Give your load test a descriptive name in the test name section.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=243)** I'll just do simple home get, make sure the load testing resource you want to deploy the load testing resources to is selected.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=257)** In this case, I'll leave the one that's going to be created, which is new.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=263)** Next, you'll define the request details that you want to test.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=270)** Click on add request, give your request a name.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=277)** Specify the URL to reach, as well as the HTTP method you are testing.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=284)** If applicable, add any other variables, like query parameters, headers, or response variables.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=294)** For now, I won't do any of those.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=297)** Then click add.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=306)** Next, click on the load tab.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=310)** Here you'll configure the load pattern, engine instances, concurrent number of virtual users, and the test duration of your test.
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=321)** Load pattern defines how the number of virtual users will ramp up during the test.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=327)** You can choose a linear, step or spike pattern, which adjusts the number of user increases, either constantly, in gradual steps, or with a sudden increase of users respectively.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=343)** In this example, I'll test a spike load pattern.
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=348)** I'll also start with a small number of users, for example, five and a short duration for the initial tests.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=357)** I'll also do five minutes.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=363)** You'll notice an informative panel that will estimate your cost based on the chosen parameters, which is quite useful.
>
> **[6:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=372)** Select a load pattern and configure the parameters that suits your testing needs.
>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=379)** Then go back and click the test criteria tab.
>
> **[6:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=385)** Optionally, here, you can define pass-fail criteria for your test based on specific metrics.
>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=393)** For example, you can set the expected average response time to below a certain threshold like this,
>
> **[6:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=412)** or expect the error rate to be below a certain percentage.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=419)** After you've configured any pass-fail criteria, click review and create.
>
> **[7:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=426)** Review all the configuration settings that you've made.
>
> **[7:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=432)** Once you're satisfied, click create.
>
> **[7:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=438)** Azure will provision the necessary resources for your load test.
>
> **[7:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=444)** Once the resources are provisioned, your load test will start automatically.
>
> **[7:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=455)** You should be redirected to the test run page.
>
> **[7:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=458)** If not, you can click through to your test.
>
> **[7:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=463)** After the test is completed, review the results carefully.
>
> **[7:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=468)** Identify any performance bottlenecks or areas where your application struggled under load.
>
> **[7:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=476)** Look for significant increases in response time or error rates as the number of virtual users increased.
>
> **[8:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=485)** Once you're done analyzing the results, it's important to delete the load testing resources to avoid further incurring costs.
>
> **[8:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=495)** Navigate back to the load testing page in your app service.
>
> **[8:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=515)** Delete the test and associated resources.
>
> **[8:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/load-testing-on-azure-app-service?u=76281980&t=524)** Now that you've learned how to run a load test directly in Azure App Service, you can be better prepared for those viral edge-cases and sudden spikes of traffic.

>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=7)** But what if you could weave security into your existing workflow, catching vulnerabilities before they hit production?
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=15)** That's where GitHub Advanced Security for Azure DevOps comes in.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=19)** This suite of tools brings automated code, secret, and dependency scanning directly into your Azure DevOps pipelines, allowing developers to build more secure applications.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=33)** In the next few minutes, we'll explore how to use these features to proactively identify and fix potential security issues.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=43)** GitHub Advanced Security for Azure DevOps offers three key pillars.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=49)** First is code scanning.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=51)** Code scanning is a feature that uses CodeQL, a semantic code analysis engine to identify potential security vulnerabilities in your code.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=61)** This includes SQL injection, cross site scripting, and path traversal.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=67)** It analyzes your code as you commit changes and during your pull request, providing actionable alerts directly within Azure Ops.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=78)** Next, secret scanning helps prevent accidental exposure of secrets like API, keys, passwords, and connection strings in your code base.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=89)** Secret scanning automatically scans your commits and pull requests to detect these secrets, preventing them from being inadvertently exposed.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=100)** Finally, dependency scanning analyzes your project's dependencies and alerts you to any known security issues, along with recommendations for remediation, such as updating to a patched version.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=114)** Many modern applications rely on numerous open source dependencies, but these dependencies can contain known vulnerabilities.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=124)** This feature helps exactly with that.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=128)** The beauty of GitHub Advanced Security is its integration.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=132)** It works directly with your Azure DevOps repositories and pipelines, providing you with timely feedback right where you're already working.

> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=141)** Let's see how easy it is to enable and view secret scanning in Azure DevOps.

>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-essential-training-for-developers/github-advanced-security-for-azure-devops?u=76281980&t=311)** If a secret is identified in a commit, an error should show blocking you from pushing your changes.
